Handcrafted quality: Alba cinnamon is carefully rolled by skilled producers, giving it its distinctive fine-scroll appearance.       Why Is Alba Cinnamon Expensive?        Alba is considered the highest and rarest grade of Ceylon cinnamon. It is     produced from very thin, tender inner bark that must be carefully harvested,     layered and hand-rolled into fine quills. Because only a small portion of     the harvest qualifies for Alba grade, supply is limited and production is     labour-intensive. This scarcity, skill and quality make Alba cinnamon more     expensive than standard cinnamon sticks or powder. Marine collagen peptides are collagen proteins that have been hydrolysed     (broken down) into smaller amino acid chains called peptides. This process     makes them easier for the body to digest and absorb.            Marine collagen is particularly rich in amino acids such as     glycine, proline and hydroxyproline, which are key structural     building blocks used by the body in collagen production and connective tissue support.            Compared to some other collagen sources, marine collagen is often preferred     for beauty and skin-focused wellness routines because of its naturally high     Type I collagen content and excellent absorption profile.       Why Is Marine Collagen More Expensive?        Marine collagen is one of the most premium collagen sources available due to     its specialised extraction process, sustainable marine sourcing and high     peptide purity.            Hydrolysed marine collagen peptides are carefully processed to create smaller,     highly bioavailable peptides that dissolve easily and absorb efficiently.     Sustainable sourcing, marine certification standards and purification also     contribute to the higher price compared to standard gelatine or lower-grade collagen products. For years, South Africa has been deprived of truly genuine, freshly harvested     saffron, often settling for old, low-quality imports that arrive months or     even years after harvest — and are sometimes adulterated. Sir Francis introduces certified authentic     ISO 3632 Certified Saffron (Crocus sativus) in     South Africa, backed by certificates of authenticity, origin and independent     lab verification.       A Rare Spice of Luxury, Wellness & Culinary Excellence        This rare spice is a culinary indulgence long celebrated for its antioxidant     power, mood support, restorative qualities and unmistakable aroma, colour     and flavour.            Harvested in the world’s most fertile saffron valleys, each strand is     rigorously evaluated for crocin (colour),     picrocrocin (flavour) and safranal     (aroma), ensuring proven authenticity and premium quality.       Premium Presentation        Presented in a striking luxury glass vial filled with all-red saffron threads     and boxed in a deluxe black drawer box, this saffron delivers exceptional     visual appeal for retail displays, premium culinary collections and gifting. ISO 3632 certified: Independently tested for authenticity and quality.     A+ grade quality: Deep crimson stigmas with intense aroma, colour and flavour.     All-red threads: Premium saffron with no yellow or pale filler strands.     Rich in antioxidants: Naturally contains crocin, picrocrocin and safranal.     Mood & wellbeing support: Traditionally used for mood, energy and restorative wellness routines.     Premium culinary use: Ideal for tea, rice dishes, desserts, baking and golden milk.     Freshness protected: Sealed and boxed to protect from air, light and moisture.     Luxury gifting format: Glass vial and deluxe drawer box presentation.       Usage Guide    For Your Kitchen        Steep saffron threads in warm water, milk or broth for 10–15 minutes.     Use in rice, stews, soups, desserts and drinks for richness, depth and fragrance.       For Wellness Use        Suggested dosage: 10–12 premium saffron threads,     approximately 30 mg per day.       Preparation Method for Maximum Potency               Lightly crush the threads.       This helps release more crocin, saffron’s main colour and active compound.                 Soak in cold purified water.       Place the crushed threads in 10 ml cold purified water for 1–2 hours to soften.                 Add hot water.       Pour into 150 ml hot water. Do not exceed 85°C, as higher temperatures may       damage delicate aromatic compounds such as safranal.                 Steep covered for 15 minutes.       Keep covered to preserve volatile aroma compounds.                 Consume immediately.       Drink with the threads, as they may still contain beneficial plant compounds.                 Tip: For better absorption, take after breakfast with healthy     fats such as milk, or alongside omega-3s.       When to Expect Results                        Subtle Benefits         May be noticed immediately                       Noticeable Improvements         Approximately 30 days                       Significant Results         90 days or longer with consistent use                   How to Verify Genuine Saffron               Taste & Colour Test: Chew a thread gently. Genuine saffron       is slightly bitter and tints saliva with a natural hue.                 Aroma Test: True saffron has a sweet-floral,       earthy-bitter fragrance with a strong aroma when opened. Low-grade or       adulterated saffron often has little to no scent.                 Visual Test: Authentic saffron shows a distinct       trumpet-shaped crimson stigma. Fakes are often straight, flat, crushed or       uniformly cut fibres.                 Infusion Test: In warm water, true saffron releases colour       slowly and evenly, producing a clear golden-yellow infusion. Instant red or       orange staining may indicate dye or adulteration.            Caution        Do not exceed 1 g per day. Not advised during pregnancy without medical     advice. Consult a registered healthcare professional before use if pregnant,     breastfeeding, taking medication or managing a medical condition. Use of this product is not     intended to compensate for diagnosis, treatment, cure or mitigation of     medical conditions and must not substitute advice from a registered health     professional for any health or health-related conditions.
